          <div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;text-align:left;">

        <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
          <ul>
           <li class="nv-view">
            <a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_Brazil" title="Template:Politics of Brazil">
             <abbr title="View this template">
              v
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-talk">
            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_Brazil" title="Template talk:Politics of Brazil">
             <abbr title="Discuss this template">
              t
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-edit">
            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_Brazil&amp;action=edit">
             <abbr title="Edit this template">
              e
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        impeachment of Dilma Rousseff
       </b>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Brazil" title="List of Presidents of Brazil">
        36th
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">
        President of Brazil
       </a>
       , began on 2 December 2015 with a petition for her impeachment accepted by
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Cunha" title="Eduardo Cunha">
        Eduardo Cunha
       </a>
       , then president of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_(Brazil)" title="Chamber of Deputies (Brazil)">
        Chamber of Deputies
       </a>
       , and continued into late 2016.
       <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">
        Rousseff
       </a>
       , more than 12 months into her second four-year term, was charged with criminal administrative misconduct and disregard for the federal budget in violation of article 85, items V and VI of the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">
        Constitution of Brazil
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fiscal_Responsibility_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fiscal Responsibility Law (page does not exist)">
        Fiscal Responsibility Law
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lei_de_Responsabilidade_Fiscal" title="pt:Lei de Responsabilidade Fiscal">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       , article 36.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SL101_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SL101-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The petition also accused Rousseff of criminal responsibility for failing to act on the scandal at Brazilian national petroleum company,
       <a href="/wiki/Petrobras" title="Petrobras">
        Petrobras
       </a>
       , on account of allegations uncovered by the
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Car_Wash" title="Operation Car Wash">
        Operation Car Wash
       </a>
       investigation, and for failing to distance herself from the suspects in that investigation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-request_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-request-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rousseff was president of the Petrobras board of directors during the period covered by the investigation, and approved Petrobras' controversial acquisition of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pasadena_Refining_System" title="Pasadena Refining System">
        Pasadena Refining System
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-request_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-request-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the Petrobras charges were not included in the impeachment because Prosecutor-General
       <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_Janot" title="Rodrigo Janot">
        Rodrigo Janot
       </a>
       successfully argued that a sitting president could not be investigated while in office for crimes committed prior to election.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rousseff was formally impeached on 17 April 2016. On 12 May, the Senate voted to suspend Rousseff's powers for the duration of the trial, and Vice President
       <a href="/wiki/Michel_Temer" title="Michel Temer">
        Michel Temer
       </a>
       became acting president.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBC-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 31 August 2016, the Senate removed President Rousseff from office by a 61–20 vote, finding her guilty of breaking Brazil's budget laws. Accordingly, Temer was sworn in as the 37th President of Brazil.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-auto-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Temer was accused by an Odebrecht executive of soliciting campaign donations in 2014 for his party.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He faced trial along with Rousseff in the
       <a href="/wiki/Superior_Electoral_Court" title="Superior Electoral Court">
        Superior Electoral Court
       </a>
       (TSE) in a complaint filed by
       <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9cio_Neves" title="Aécio Neves">
        Aécio Neves
       </a>
       , the candidate narrowly defeated by Rousseff in the 2014 presidential
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_general_election,_2014" title="Brazilian general election, 2014">
        runoff
       </a>
       , over irregularities in their campaign funds—Rousseff had shared the
       <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_(Brazil)" title="Workers' Party (Brazil)">
        PT
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Democratic_Movement" title="Brazilian Democratic Movement">
        PMDB
       </a>
       coalition ticket with Temer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 9 June 2017 the court rejected, by a 4–3 vote, the allegations of campaign finance violations by the Rousseff-Temer ticket during the 2014 electoral campaign. As a result of that judgement, President Temer has remained in office and both Rousseff and Temer have retained their political rights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSEVote_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-TSEVote-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Background">
        Background
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span id="Petrobras_and_.22fiscal_pedalling.22">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id='Petrobras_and_"fiscal_pedalling"'>
        Petrobras and "fiscal pedalling"
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title='Edit section: Petrobras and "fiscal pedalling"'>
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrobras_scandal" title="Petrobras scandal">
        Petrobras scandal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Car_Wash" title="Operation Car Wash">
        Operation Car Wash
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Solenidades._Homenagens_(16148943366).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2054" data-file-width="3087" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Solenidades._Homenagens_%2816148943366%29.jpg/240px-Solenidades._Homenagens_%2816148943366%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Solenidades._Homenagens_%2816148943366%29.jpg/360px-Solenidades._Homenagens_%2816148943366%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Solenidades._Homenagens_%2816148943366%29.jpg/480px-Solenidades._Homenagens_%2816148943366%29.jpg 2x" width="240"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Solenidades._Homenagens_(16148943366).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Rousseff speaking at her presidential inauguration to a joint session of the
         <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">
          National Congress
         </a>
         , 1 January 2015. Behind her are Senate president
         <a href="/wiki/Renan_Calheiros" title="Renan Calheiros">
          Renan Calheiros
         </a>
         , and Vice President
         <a href="/wiki/Michel_Temer" title="Michel Temer">
          Michel Temer
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Graft_(politics)" title="Graft (politics)">
        Graft
       </a>
       allegedly occurred during Rousseff's term as chair of the board of directors of the state-owned energy company Petrobras between 2003 and 2010.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="needs a source, if this is also in the BBC ref make that explicit please (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In February 2014, an investigation by the
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Police_of_Brazil" title="Federal Police of Brazil">
        Federal Police
       </a>
       , codenamed Operation Car Wash, put Petrobras at the center of "what may be the largest corruption scandal in Brazil's history".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2014_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_2014-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euromoney_2015_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Euromoney_2015-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 14 November 2014, police raids in six Brazilian states brought in several prominent Brazilian politicians and businessmen, including some Petrobras directors, who were investigated for "suspicious" contracts worth $22 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2014_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_2014-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euromoney_2015_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Euromoney_2015-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Further investigation also found offshore accounts and art collections held by those involved in the controversy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPdownfall_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WPdownfall-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       However, no evidence that Rousseff herself was involved in the Petrobras controversy has been found and she has denied any prior knowledge of the graft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNapril12_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CNNapril12-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       More than one million Brazilians protested in the streets in March 2015 calling for Rousseff's impeachment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJmarch16_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WSJmarch16-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 5 May 2016,
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court" title="Supreme Federal Court">
        Supreme Court
       </a>
       justice
       <a href="/wiki/Teori_Zavascki" title="Teori Zavascki">
        Teori Zavascki
       </a>
       dismissed counts brought against Rousseff by Senator
       <a href="/wiki/Delc%C3%ADdio_do_Amaral" title="Delcídio do Amaral">
        Delcídio do Amaral
       </a>
       based on the Petrobras controversy, ruling that a sitting president could not be investigated for actions taken before assuming office as had been argued by Prosecutor-General Rodrigo Janot.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rousseff was also accused of
       <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_pedaling" title="Fiscal pedaling">
        fiscal pedaling
       </a>
       in her administration—an accounting maneuver to give the false impression that more money was received than was spent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The government allegedly failed to fund public and private banks that managed public payments, including social assistance programs like
       <a href="/wiki/Bolsa_Fam%C3%ADlia" title="Bolsa Família">
        Bolsa Família
       </a>
       , forcing the banks to finance the programs themselves without compensation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fiscal_Pedaling_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fiscal_Pedaling-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Rousseff Administration's budgeting allegedly used this pedaling to improve its fiscal outcomes and make the surplus for the years 2012 to 2014 appear larger.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCU_conclusion_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-TCU_conclusion-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Tribunal_de_Contas_da_Uni%C3%A3o" title="Tribunal de Contas da União">
        Tribunal de Contas da União
       </a>
       (TCU), unanimously declared this maneuver a violation of fiscal responsibility.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCU_conclusion_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-TCU_conclusion-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       TCU, an auxiliary of the legislative body, has no legal power, but their decision put the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">
        National Congress
       </a>
       under great pressure to begin impeachment proceedings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_context">
        Political context
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Political context">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_protests_in_Brazil" title="2015–16 protests in Brazil">
        2015–16 protests in Brazil
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%932017_Brazilian_economic_recession" title="2014–2017 Brazilian economic recession">
        2014–2017 Brazilian economic recession
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rousseff won the 2014 general election with 51.64% of the votes in one of the most contentious presidential elections in the country's history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Sworn in on 1 January 2015,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rousseff began her second term weakened by corruption allegations as well as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%932016_Brazilian_economic_recession" title="2014–2016 Brazilian economic recession">
        2014–2016 Brazilian economic recession
       </a>
       . On 15 March 2015,
       <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_protests_in_Brazil" title="2015–16 protests in Brazil">
        protests
       </a>
       began, gathering millions of Brazilians across the country to demand among other things Rousseff's resignation or her impeachment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By June 2015 some polls reported her disapproval rating as high as 68%, the highest for any Brazilian president since the country's
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brazil_since_1985" title="History of Brazil since 1985">
        redemocratization
       </a>
       , and by August 2015 this had risen to 71%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rousseff's government was accused by the TCU of misconduct in management of public accounts since 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The President of the Chamber of Deputies, Eduardo Cunha, was investigated in Operation Car Wash for allegedly receiving bribes and keeping secret Swiss bank accounts. The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Council_of_Ethics_and_Parliamentary_Decorum_of_the_House_of_Deputies_of_Brazil&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Council of Ethics and Parliamentary Decorum of the House of Deputies of Brazil (page does not exist)">
        Council of Ethics and Parliamentary Decorum of the House of Deputies of Brazil
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conselho_de_%C3%89tica_e_Decoro_Parlamentar_da_C%C3%A2mara_dos_Deputados_do_Brasil" title="pt:Conselho de Ética e Decoro Parlamentar da Câmara dos Deputados do Brasil">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       filed a complaint against him, putting him at risk of losing his seat. The council was responsible for judging and applying penalties to deputies in cases of non-compliance with norms. Rumors emerged about attempts between Cunha's party (PMDB) and Rousseff's party to reach an agreement: that she would archive the lawsuit against Cunha if he would refuse to accept the request for her impeachment. When the Workers' Party announced to the Council of Ethics its support for the lawsuit against Cunha, he accepted the impeachment request, allegedly in retaliation. Cunha dismissed that his decision was motivated by personal or political reasons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TG_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-TG-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bargain_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bargain-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In his defence, Cunha said that opening the impeachment process was his constitutional duty as chamber president, and the decision to do so was based only on facts related to the budget laws. Cunha said further that he had no personal grievance against the Workers' Party and that Rousseff had signed six decrees for additional spending, which had increased the 2015 federal spending in non-compliance with the annual budget law and without approval of the Congress.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bargain_43-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-bargain-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rousseff denied any attempted deal to save Cunha in return for stopping her impeachment, and also denied agreements to interfere with the Council of Ethics in exchange for approval of the re-introduction of the CPMF tax (Provisional Tax on Financial Transactions), which was a wish from the government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At a news conference on 2 December 2015, she said that she would never accept or agree to any kind of corrupt bargain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UOL_1_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UOL_1-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: 50%;">
       <tr>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">
         “
        </td>
        <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">
         <small>
          I have received with indignation the decision by the head of the lower chamber to [launch] the impeachment process. There is no wrongful act committed by me, nor are there any suspicions that I have misused public money [...] The reasons given for this request [of impeachment] are inconsistent and unfounded. I have not committed any illicit act. My government performed all acts according to the principle of responsibility towards the public property, [...] I’ve committed no illicit act, there is no suspicion hanging over me of any misuse of public money. I don’t have any offshore bank accounts, I have no hidden assets. [...] I would never accept any kind of bargain, much less those that threaten the free functioning of democratic institutions in this country.
         </small>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">
         ”
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td class="cquotecite" colspan="3" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; text-align: right;">
         <cite>
          —
          <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">
           Dilma Rousseff
          </a>
          , television news 2 December 2015.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UOL_1_45-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-UOL_1-45">
            [45]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
           <a href="#cite_note-46">
            [46]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
           <a href="#cite_note-47">
            [47]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TG_40-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-TG-40">
            [40]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </cite>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       After this pronouncement by the president, Cunha said Rousseff had lied to the nation when she said she would not participate in any deal and that her government had much to explain to the country. Cunha claimed he was not aware of any negotiations and that he had never met
       <a href="/wiki/Jaques_Wagner" title="Jaques Wagner">
        Jaques Wagner
       </a>
       , the supposed intermediary in the alleged negotiations with Rousseff. Declaring his opposition to the Workers' Party, he said he would rather forgo their three votes in the Council of Ethics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: 40%;">
       <tr>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">
         “
        </td>
        <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">
         <small>
          She lied on national television network and this is very serious. If she had not participated directly I would not speak.
         </small>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">
         ”
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td class="cquotecite" colspan="3" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; text-align: right;">
         <cite>
          —
          <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Cunha" title="Eduardo Cunha">
           Eduardo Cunha
          </a>
          , News conference – 3 December 2015.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bargain_43-2">
           <a href="#cite_note-bargain-43">
            [43]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Translation" title="Wikipedia:Translation">
             <span title="This translation of a non-English text into English lacks translator's reference.">
              whose translation?
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
         </cite>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Comments_by_specialists_and_public_opinion">
        Comments by specialists and public opinion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Comments by specialists and public opinion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Professor Leonardo Avritzer of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidade_Federal_de_Minas_Gerais" title="Universidade Federal de Minas Gerais">
        Universidade Federal de Minas Gerais
       </a>
       told
       <a href="/wiki/Ag%C3%AAncia_Brasil" title="Agência Brasil">
        Agência Brasil
       </a>
       in December 2015 that the political crisis was tied to Rousseff's inability to negotiate with Congress, and that Brazil's fragmented political system (and many
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Brazil" title="List of political parties in Brazil">
        political parties
       </a>
       ) had created an ungovernable government. According to him, the
       <a href="/wiki/Opposition_(politics)" title="Opposition (politics)">
        opposition
       </a>
       confronting Rousseff after the 2014 elections calling for a recount and her disputed campaign accounts, culminating in the impeachment process, had been other major factors in the destabilization of the government. However, political scientist Luciana Veiga stated that, at that time, the process was benefiting Rousseff, who was now free from blackmail and could potentially reorganize her government. Veiga believed that Cunha could be removed from office and that the opposition would try to push the impeachment process of Rousseff in Congress for 2016 in order to mitigate the "electoral ecstasy" and "act of revenge" that were said to be the cause of the impeachment attempt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Terra_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Terra-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In CNT/MDA polls conducted in March 2015, only 10.8% of Brazilians approved of Rousseff's government and 59.7% wanted her impeached.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-REUTjuly21_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-REUTjuly21-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By July 2015, the latter number had risen to 62.8%. Similar data were collected by the
       <a href="/wiki/Datafolha" title="Datafolha">
        Datafolha Institute
       </a>
       in April 2016, showing that 61% of Brazilians believed that Rousseff should be impeached.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTapr11_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYTapr11-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Request_for_impeachment">
        Request for impeachment
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Request for impeachment">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       A total of 37 requests for the impeachment of Rousseff had been presented to the Chamber of Deputies from 2012 till her actual impeachment. Of these 23 were archived and did not proceed. The remaining 14 proceeded, but only one was accepted by Cunha.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-request_4-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-request-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Submitted by former congressman and attorney
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=H%C3%A9lio_Bicudo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hélio Bicudo (page does not exist)">
        Hélio Bicudo
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/H%C3%A9lio_Bicudo" title="pt:Hélio Bicudo">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       and attorneys
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Reale_J%C3%BAnior&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Miguel Reale Júnior (page does not exist)">
        Miguel Reale Júnior
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miguel_Reale_J%C3%BAnior" title="pt:Miguel Reale Júnior">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Janaina_Paschoal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Janaina Paschoal (page does not exist)">
        Janaina Paschoal
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janaina_Paschoal" title="pt:Janaina Paschoal">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       , it was based on allegations of omission concerning the Petrobras controversy, fiscal responsibility crimes, and budgetary mismanagement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FT-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Omission">
        Omission
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Omission">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The illegal or suspicious transactions investigated by Operation Car Wash included the purchase of Pasadena Refinery by Petrobras, a deal that cost it R$792 million (US$362 million).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rousseff chaired the board of directors of Petrobras when the purchase was approved. She later said that a mistake had been made concerning a contractual clause and that "her decision was based on a technically and legally flawed summary" of the purchase document drawn up by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nestor_Cerver%C3%B3&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nestor Cerveró (page does not exist)">
        Nestor Cerveró
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nestor_Cerver%C3%B3" title="pt:Nestor Cerveró">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       , the financial director of
       <a href="/wiki/Petrobras_Distribuidora" title="Petrobras Distribuidora">
        Petrobras Distribuidora
       </a>
       (the fuel distribution and trading subsidiary of Petrobras).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WT_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WT-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Petrobras paid Astra Oil, a wholly owned subsidiary of Astro Oil Trading NV, $360 million for 50% of Pasadena Refining System.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A year later, Astra exercised a
       <a href="/wiki/Put_option" title="Put option">
        put option
       </a>
       that required Petrobras to buy out the other half, then won the arbitration case over the deal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WT_57-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-WT-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cerveró was later convicted of money laundering and sentenced to five years in jail.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The president called the allegations a kind of coup and merely an attempt to weaken Petrobras.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Emphasizing its expertise in the economy and energy sectors, the president stressed the company's financial health. She stepped down from the Petrobras board only in February 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some international companies were chosen to be encouraged and, thereafter participated in unrealistic bids to drain the state-owned company, giving back much of the value through seemingly licit donations.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title='Why "seemingly"? (June 2017)'>
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       It was alleged that statements taken from the accused in Operation Car Wash suggested that Lula and Rousseff had known of the bribery scheme in Petrobras.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fiscal_responsibility_crimes">
        Fiscal responsibility crimes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Fiscal responsibility crimes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Rousseff issued six unnumbered decrees in 2014 and 2015 that allocated funds to social programs, allegedly for political purposes, without authorization from Congress. These totaled R$18.5 billion (US$6.9 billion) and were contracted in official financial institutions with neither the necessary legislative authorization, nor targets which complied with the Lei de Responsabilidade Fiscal (Fiscal Responsibility Law) and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Annual_Budgetary_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Annual Budgetary Law (page does not exist)">
        Annual Budgetary Law
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lei_or%C3%A7ament%C3%A1ria_anual" title="pt:Lei orçamentária anual">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       . To obtain these additional credits, the target of 2014 was reduced by the end of 2014 by R$67 billion (US$25 billion) at the request of the president. Rousseff allegedly committed similar crimes of fiscal irresponsibility in 2015. She further issued such decrees in the years 2014 and 2015 to authorize the opening credit precisely to, purportedly, allow the provision of additional resources despite it being known that the primary
       <i>
        superavit
       </i>
       target in the budget forecast was not being fulfilled, and would not be fulfilled, hence disregarding the Annual Budgetary Law and the Federal Constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id=".22Fiscal_pedaling.22">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id='"Fiscal_pedaling"'>
        "Fiscal pedaling"
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title='Edit section: "Fiscal pedaling"'>
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 2011 and 2014, Rousseff's government is said to have held illegal credit operations, using funds from the state-owned banks
       <a href="/wiki/Caixa_Econ%C3%B4mica_Federal" title="Caixa Econômica Federal">
        Caixa Econômica Federal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Banco_do_Brasil" title="Banco do Brasil">
        Banco do Brasil
       </a>
       to finance social programs without officially declaring loans from either of those banks, an example of fiscal pedaling. These transactions were reported in 2015 by the TCU and, according to the report, were undertaken in order to improve the government's chances of re-election.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Caixa Econômica Federal and Banco do Brasil operated federal social programs under a government contract at this time. The government would pass the funds necessary to finance the programs through the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Secretariat_of_the_National_Treasury&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Secretariat of the National Treasury (page does not exist)">
        Secretariat of the National Treasury
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretaria_do_Tesouro_Nacional" title="pt:Secretaria do Tesouro Nacional">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       every month. They were obliged to transfer the equivalent values for the equalization of interest rates, expenditures and legal transfers covered under the contract. But the government had not made these reimbursements, and the contracted banks instead funded the programs using their own capital, capital that the government was obliged to reimburse them for, although no loans had been officially filed. The Fiscal Responsibility Law (Article 36) prohibits members of the federal government who control state financial institutions from borrowing from those institutions that they control.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SL101_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-SL101-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The total balance of these liabilities by the end of August 2014 was R$1.74 billion (US$740 million). Of the total R$7.8 billion (US$2.9 billion) spent on subsidies in these programs between 2009 and 2014, only R$1.6 billion (US$590 million) was transferred by the Government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At the end of 2014, Rousseff sent the Congress
       <a href="/wiki/Bill_(law)" title="Bill (law)">
        PLN
       </a>
       362014, to change the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Budgetary_Directives_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Budgetary Directives Law (page does not exist)">
        Budgetary Directives Law
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lei_de_diretrizes_or%C3%A7ament%C3%A1rias" title="pt:Lei de diretrizes orçamentárias">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       in order to modify the rules of the primary
       <i>
        superavit
       </i>
       (surplus), and hence showing her knowledge of the fiscal pedaling by taking steps to normalize the accounts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Process_in_Congress">
        Process in Congress
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Process in Congress">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Request_for_impeachment_2">
        Request for impeachment
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Request for impeachment">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Entrevistas_Diversas_(23181337800).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Entrevistas_Diversas_%2823181337800%29.jpg/230px-Entrevistas_Diversas_%2823181337800%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Entrevistas_Diversas_%2823181337800%29.jpg/345px-Entrevistas_Diversas_%2823181337800%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Entrevistas_Diversas_%2823181337800%29.jpg/460px-Entrevistas_Diversas_%2823181337800%29.jpg 2x" width="230"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Entrevistas_Diversas_(23181337800).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Cunha" title="Eduardo Cunha">
          Eduardo Cunha
         </a>
         stating that the Chamber of Deputies had agreed to open the proceedings, on 2 December 2015.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       By September 2015, 37 requests for impeachment had been filed with the Chamber of Deputies against Rousseff, but Cunha did not accept any, except for that of Hélio Bicudo and lawyers Miguel Reale Júnior and Janaina Paschoal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-request_4-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-request-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Much of the pro-impeachment movement (including the
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Brazil_Movement" title="Free Brazil Movement">
        Free Brazil
       </a>
       group and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Come_to_the_Street_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Come to the Street Movement (page does not exist)">
        Come to the Street Movement
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Movimento_Vem_pra_Rua" title="pt:Movimento Vem pra Rua">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       ) joined Bicudo's request.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Congressmen supportive of the impeachment also organized a
       <a href="/wiki/Petition" title="Petition">
        petition
       </a>
       in its favor, which garnered the signatures of two million Brazilians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Documents presented to the House attempted to implicate Rousseff in the controversy uncovered by Operation Car Wash, citing a failure to investigate corruption allegations against former President
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luiz_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Lula da Silva">
        Luiz Lula da Silva
       </a>
       , in addition to those and other allegations against herself.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-El_País_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-El_País-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The six decrees which were the subject of many of those allegations of fiscal pedaling and which Rousseff had unilaterally pushed into law were also entered as evidence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Voting_in_the_Chamber_committee">
        Voting in the Chamber committee
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Voting in the Chamber committee">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       A special committee formed in the Chamber of Deputies voted on 11 April 2016 on the petition's admissibility, at the same time that 37 of the 65 committee members were also facing charges of corruption or other crimes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LA-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Testimony by the authors of the request was followed by Rousseff's defense. Meanwhile, street protests both for and against the impeachment occurred throughout the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The committee eventually voted 38 to 27 for impeachment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable plainrowheaders sortable" style="text-align:right;">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Senate_vote_on_suspension">
        Senate vote on suspension
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Senate vote on suspension">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          <b>
           This section needs expansion
          </b>
          .
          <small>
           You can help by
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">
            adding to it
           </a>
           .
          </small>
          <small>
           <i>
            (May 2016)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist">
         Wikinews has related news:
         <i>
          <b>
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Brazilian_Senate_vote_to_suspend_President_Rousseff" title="wikinews:Brazilian Senate vote to suspend President Rousseff">
            Brazilian Senate vote to suspend President Rousseff
           </a>
          </b>
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       After it passed out of committee, the full lower house also voted in favor of impeachment, 367 for and 137 against, with 342 necessary for it to pass (7 abstaining, 2 absent).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       But similarly to the situation in committee, 303 of the 513 members of the lower house were facing criminal charges or investigation at the time of the vote.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_76-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-LA-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cunha then referred the matter to the Senate which eventually, after a session of more than twenty hours on 12 May, resolved to suspend Rousseff's presidential powers and duties for up to 180 days, a motion which passed 55–22. During the judicial process leading up to the Senate vote on impeachment, then Vice President Michel Temer served as acting president.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBC-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       But before that, on 5 May 2016, Teori Zavascki, judge of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court_(Brazil)" title="Supreme Federal Court (Brazil)">
        Supreme Federal Court
       </a>
       ruled that Cunha must step down as president of the Chamber, because he faced a corruption trial. The decision was later endorsed by all eleven judges of the Court but nevertheless did not affect the process of impeachment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 12 September 2016, Cunha was finally ousted from the Chamber with his political rights suspended under accusation of lying in testimony to the committee investigating Operation Car Wash allegations, the culmination of an internal investigation that had lasted eleven months.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 19 October 2016, Cunha was arrested on charges of corruption and bribery related to a Petrobras
       <a href="/wiki/Drillship" title="Drillship">
        drillship
       </a>
       purchase.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_president">
        Acting president
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Acting president">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Car_Wash" title="Operation Car Wash">
        Operation Car Wash
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2444" data-file-width="4131" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg/280px-Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg/420px-Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg/560px-Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Michel Temer in his first ministerial meeting on 13 May 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the Brazilian political system, the president and vice president run on the same ticket but have constitutionally separate terms. Michel Temer, who was president of the Chamber during the
       <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Henrique_Cardoso" title="Fernando Henrique Cardoso">
        Fernando Henrique Cardoso
       </a>
       presidency from 1995 to 2003, is a member of the Brazilian Democratic Movement Party (PMDB), which announced it was running against the Rousseff government in March 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to
       <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">
        the Guardian
       </a>
       ,
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        "...for those desperate for change, Temer represents salvation. Others, more concerned about the country's fragile democracy, believe he is the perpetrator of a coup."
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
         <a href="#cite_note-89">
          [89]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       A separate
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impeachment_proposal_against_Michel_Temer" title="Impeachment proposal against Michel Temer">
        proposal
       </a>
       sought to impeach Temer, the official process having started on 6 April 2016 when Cunha formed a commission to investigate one impeachment request among the five made against Temer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In March 2017, former
       <a href="/wiki/Odebrecht" title="Odebrecht">
        Odebrecht Group
       </a>
       CEO
       <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Odebrecht" title="Marcelo Odebrecht">
        Marcelo Odebrecht
       </a>
       , as part of a
       <a href="/wiki/Plea_bargain" title="Plea bargain">
        plea bargain
       </a>
       for leniency, said before the Superior Electoral Court Judge Herman Benjamin, that PMDB and PT
       <a href="/wiki/Slush_fund" title="Slush fund">
        slush funds
       </a>
       received payments of R$150 million (US$48 million) from Odebrecht's construction conglomerate for the 2014 re-election campaign in 2014, and that at least a third of the money originated from corrupt practices. Odebrecht was jailed in June 2015 for corruption uncovered by Operation Car Wash.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">
        Public opinion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Public opinion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       A CNT/MDA poll published on 8 June 2016, indicated that only 11.3% of Brazilians approved while 28% disapproved of the acting government of President Temer. For 30.2% of respondents, Temer's government is ordinary, while 30.5% gave no answer. The survey also showed that 46.6% of Brazilians believed that the corruption in Temer's government could equal that in Rousseff's government. 28.3% believed that corruption could be less and the remaining 18.6% estimated that it could be even greater. Regarding the lawfulness of the process of impeachment, 61.5% agreed with the conduct of the process, 33.3% answered negatively and 5.2% didn't answer. CNT/MDA polled 2,002 people in 137 municipalities in 25 federative units between 2 and 5 June. CNT/MDA reported the poll as 95% reliable with a 2% margin of error.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       An
       <a href="/wiki/Ipsos" title="Ipsos">
        Ipsos
       </a>
       poll in early July 2016 investigated what outcome most Brazilians were hoping for, with mixed results: 16% of Brazilians preferred Temer in office; 20% said that Rousseff should be acquitted and finish her four-year mandate; and 52% said that whoever assumed the presidency should call new elections for president. However, holding new elections would only be possible with a 3/5 majority in both houses of congress. Alternatively, both could have been removed from office, depending on the outcome of a lawsuit filed in the Superior Electoral Court by the
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Social_Democracy_Party" title="Brazilian Social Democracy Party">
        PSDB
       </a>
       , party of Aécio Neves, the defeated candidate in the 2014 presidential elections, whose suit alleged electoral crime by the political alliance of Rousseff-Temer involving donations from the companies implicated in Operation Car Wash.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Impeachment_trial">
        Impeachment trial
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Impeachment trial">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       After the Senate vote to suspend Rousseff's presidential powers and duties, subsequent procedure required new citations, new defense, appointing witnesses and producing evidence for preparation of the final report, which first of all had to be reviewed by a committee and then the entire Senate, each requiring a simple majority to confirm that the charges were well-founded. After that, the debate over conviction or acquittal began, requiring a two-thirds majority of the Senate, which proceedings were chaired by
       <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lewandowski" title="Ricardo Lewandowski">
        Ricardo Lewandowski
       </a>
       . This eventually resulted in Rousseff's permanent removal, the appeal of which was denied by the court.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial_99-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-trial-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Rousseff.27s_defense">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rousseff's_defense">
        Rousseff's defense
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Rousseff's defense">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Rousseff had 20 days to present a preliminary written defense for the trial in the Senate and Rousseff's lawyer
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_Cardozo" title="José Eduardo Cardozo">
        José Eduardo Cardozo
       </a>
       did so on 1 June 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_Cardozo_CEI2016.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2424" data-file-width="3240" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_Cardozo_CEI2016.jpg/200px-Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_Cardozo_CEI2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_Cardozo_CEI2016.jpg/300px-Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_Cardozo_CEI2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_Cardozo_CEI2016.jpg/400px-Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_Cardozo_CEI2016.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_Cardozo_CEI2016.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <center>
          José Eduardo Cardozo, lawyer who represented Rousseff
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       His 370-page filing said that the president had not committed the alleged crimes and that Rousseff's impeachment "was solely and exclusively aimed at ending Operation Car Wash." Cardozo submitted as evidence transcripts of a recorded telephone conversation between
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_S%C3%A9rgio_Machado&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="José Sérgio Machado (page does not exist)">
        José Sérgio Machado
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/S%C3%A9rgio_Machado_(pol%C3%ADtico_e_empres%C3%A1rio)" title="pt:Sérgio Machado (político e empresário)">
         pt
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       , former president of Petrobras subsidiary
       <a href="/wiki/Transpetro" title="Transpetro">
        Transpetro
       </a>
       , and Senator
       <a href="/wiki/Romero_Juc%C3%A1" title="Romero Jucá">
        Romero Jucá
       </a>
       , an influential politician in the PMDB. Published by the newspaper
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Folha_de_S._Paulo" title="Folha de S. Paulo">
        Folha de S. Paulo
       </a>
       , the conversation convinced Cardozo that the two were trying to prevent the investigation from widening, due to the risk to both of being caught up in it, and suggested that Rousseff's impeachment could have been part of an agreement aimed at preventing (and possibly later stopping) the Operation Car Wash investigations.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="allegations of criminality require a solid reference even though sourced. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Jucá's lawyer said that his client never thought to interfere in Operation Car Wash and that the dialogue did not suggest that he did.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Jucá, who had been appointed
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Planning,_Budget,_and_Management" title="Ministry of Planning, Budget, and Management">
        Planning Minister
       </a>
       by Temer, also denied ever attempting to obstruct the investigation, and after speaking with Temer on 23 May, said that he had no intention of resigning.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the next day Jucá stepped down after eleven days in office.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Committee_meetings">
        Committee meetings
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Committee meetings">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Work_plan_and_preliminary_requests">
        Work plan and preliminary requests
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Work plan and preliminary requests">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       On 25 May 2016, Senator
       <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B4nio_Anastasia" title="Antônio Anastasia">
        Antônio Anastasia
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Rapporteur" title="Rapporteur">
         rapporteur
        </a>
       </i>
       of the Special Committee of Impeachment 2016 (CEI 2016),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       presented a work plan for the trial. The next meeting was scheduled for 2 June, to analyze new deadlines.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial_99-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-trial-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The committee assessed Anastasia's report and work plan deadlines, and requests by senators
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       , on 2 June 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in a session that lasted over nine hours. Anastasia proposed that final arguments be heard by 7 July. Anastasia ruled against recorded telephone conversation between Machado and Jucá being introduced into evidence, ruling it irrelevant since the charges against Rousseff were fiscal responsibility crimes and the recording was only an informal conversation and proved nothing in law. Cardozo protested that the facts cited in the recording were a primary question of the investigation, and announced on 3 June that he would appeal the decision to the president of the Supreme Court.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The committee approved the work plan and deadlines on 6 June.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 7 June, Lewandowski denied the appeal filed by Cardozo to append the recording of Sérgio Machado, citing a precedent that evidence of that type is confidential until the beginning of a formal investigation. Machado was arrested and introduced the recording of the conversation during his interrogation. The subject under appeal had been discussed in prior decisions of the Court.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Lewandowski also denied an appeal by senator
       <a href="/wiki/Aloysio_Nunes" title="Aloysio Nunes">
        Aloysio Nunes
       </a>
       , former member of the Committee, to reduce the number of witnesses.
      </p>
      <p>
       At the 2 June meeting, the Committee had established that eight witnesses would be heard for each of the six supplemental budget decrees against Rousseff, both for the prosecution and for the defense, i.e. a total of 48 witnesses for each side, with each decree considered separately. Nunes contended that the six decrees should be considered a single entity, to be added to the so-called "tax pedaling", so that the number of witnesses to be heard could be reduced to 16.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jana%C3%ADna_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Paschoal_CEI2016.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2250" data-file-width="2790" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Jana%C3%ADna_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Paschoal_CEI2016.jpg/200px-Jana%C3%ADna_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Paschoal_CEI2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Jana%C3%ADna_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Paschoal_CEI2016.jpg/300px-Jana%C3%ADna_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Paschoal_CEI2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Jana%C3%ADna_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Paschoal_CEI2016.jpg/400px-Jana%C3%ADna_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Paschoal_CEI2016.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jana%C3%ADna_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Paschoal_CEI2016.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <center>
          Janaína Conceição Paschoal, prosecutor
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 8 June, the committee accepted a request by both defense and prosecution reducing to four the number of supplemental budget decrees to be considered in the trial. Thus, the number of witnesses in the process was reduced to forty. Since each charge entitled eight witnesses, the defense of Rousseff could introduce up to 32 witnesses for the four decrees and eight for the "tax pedaling" charge. The prosecution would be entitled to the same number. The decision to reduce the charges was supported by a report produced at the House of Representatives, which considered that two decrees signed by Rousseff without approval of Congress were neutral from a fiscal perspective, once the primary sources and financial expenses listed in the documents were equivalent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Witnesses">
        Witnesses
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Witnesses">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The hearings began on 8 June 2016 with four prosecution witnesses. The prosecutors were
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jana%C3%ADna_Paschoal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Janaína Paschoal (page does not exist)">
        Janaína Paschoal
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
